         <div class="really_simple_share_stumbleupon" style="width:80px;">
          <script src="https://www.stumbleupon.com/hostedbadge.php?s=1&amp;r=http://www.eatthelove.com/2014/01/korean-fried-chicken-recipe/" type="text/javascript">
          </script>
         </div>
         <div class="really_simple_share_reddit" style="width:110px;">
          <script src="http://1-ps.googleusercontent.com/xk/K6gBah9QXywmHQxDJ7YfEI4z86/www.eatthelove.com/www.reddit.com/static/button/button1.js,qnewwindow=1,aurl=,hwww.eatthelove.com,_2014,_01,_korean-fried-chicken-recipe,_.pagespeed.jm.64dhltEBDEXbfxjtyrkG.js" type="text/javascript">
          </script>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="really_simple_share_clearfix">
        </div>
        <p>
         This insanely easy, super addictive Korean Fried Chicken Recipe is baked in the oven not deep-fried but still creates a super crisp skin!
        </p>
        <p>
         <a href="http://www.eatthelove.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/Korean-Fried-Chicken-Recipe.jpg">
          <img alt="Korean Fried Chicken Recipe. Photo and recipe by Irvin Lin of Eat the Love. www.eatthelove.com" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-10802" height="810" src="http://www.eatthelove.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/Korean-Fried-Chicken-Recipe.jpg" width="540"/>
         </a>
        </p>
        <p>
         Oh Man! Is that what we missed?!? said my sister when she saw
         <a href="http://instagram.com/p/jFlIPfvSiF/" target="_blank">
          AJ post a picture
         </a>
         of the Korean Fried Chicken Recipe that I had made. I originally had plans to make the Korean Fried Chicken when they were visiting but a flight cancellation and a reshuffling of family events meant I wouldnt time to make them for everyone. Just as well, because that meant more for AJ and me! (
         <a href="#recipe">
          Jump directly to the recipe.
         </a>
         )
        </p>
        <p>
         <a href="http://www.eatthelove.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/Korean-Fried-Chicken-Recipe-2.jpg">
          <img alt="Korean Fried Chicken. Recipe and Photo by Irvin Lin of Eat the Love. www.eatthelove.com" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-10799" height="360" onerror="this.onerror=null;pagespeed.lazyLoadImages.loadIfVisibleAndMaybeBeacon(this);" onload="pagespeed.lazyLoadImages.loadIfVisibleAndMaybeBeacon(this);" pagespeed_lazy_src="http://www.eatthelove.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/Korean-Fried-Chicken-Recipe-2.jpg" src="//1-ps.googleusercontent.com/hk/N7MgqQe61PieTxdAHj4St7PAZ5/www.gstatic.com/psa/static/1.gif" width="540"/>
         </a>
         <span id="more-10797">
         </span>
         <br/>
         The first time I had Korean Fried Chicken, which those in-the-know refer to as the other KFC was in New York with my friend Calvin. I had coincidentally arrived in the city for a conference that also coincided with his birthday. He rounded up a few friends and we all headed to Korea Town to get Korean Fried Chicken at
         <a href="http://madforchicken.com/" target="_blank">
          Mad for Chicken
         </a>
         . Spicy and sweet with a shatteringly crispy skin, I was immediately smitten.
        </p>
        <p>
         <a href="http://www.eatthelove.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/Korean-Fried-Chicken-Recipe-1.jpg">
          <img alt="Korean Fried Chicken with sweet and spicy sauce. Photo and recipe by Irvin Lin of Eat the Love. www.eatthelove.com" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-10798" height="810" onerror="this.onerror=null;pagespeed.lazyLoadImages.loadIfVisibleAndMaybeBeacon(this);" onload="pagespeed.lazyLoadImages.loadIfVisibleAndMaybeBeacon(this);" pagespeed_lazy_src="http://www.eatthelove.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/Korean-Fried-Chicken-Recipe-1.jpg" src="//1-ps.googleusercontent.com/hk/N7MgqQe61PieTxdAHj4St7PAZ5/www.gstatic.com/psa/static/1.gif" width="540"/>
         </a>
        </p>
        <p>
         Traditionally you make KFC by double frying the chicken. Much like a French fry, the double frying of the chicken results in a super crisp brittle skin that snaps and cracks the second you bite into it, coated with deep, rich sweet and spicy sauce (or a sweet and garlic filled soy sauce for those who dont like the heat). Im not afraid of deep-frying but then I found a recipe by the innovative folks behind the blog
         <a href="http://ideasinfood.com/" target="_blank">
          Ideas in Food
         </a>
         . Their cookbook Maximum Flavor had a technique for first coating the chicken in a salt, baking soda, egg white mixture and letting it dry out in the refrigerator. Unorthodox in nature I was pretty impressed with how they turned out, especially since it could just stick the chicken in the oven, and not have to deal with all the oil. Easy Korean Fried Chicken, oven baked! Im so making these all the time now.
        </p>
        <p>
         <a href="http://www.eatthelove.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/Korean-Fried-Chicken-Recipe-4.jpg">
          <img alt="Korean Fried Chicken baked in the oven! Recipe and Photo by Irvin Lin of Eat the Love. www.eatthelove.com" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-10801" height="810" onerror="this.onerror=null;pagespeed.lazyLoadImages.loadIfVisibleAndMaybeBeacon(this);" onload="pagespeed.lazyLoadImages.loadIfVisibleAndMaybeBeacon(this);" pagespeed_lazy_src="http://www.eatthelove.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/Korean-Fried-Chicken-Recipe-4.jpg" src="//1-ps.googleusercontent.com/hk/N7MgqQe61PieTxdAHj4St7PAZ5/www.gstatic.com/psa/static/1.gif" width="540"/>
         </a>
        </p>
        <p>
         <em>
          Be sure to visit Eat the Love all this week. Ill be posting a new chicken wings recipe each day from Monday, January 20th to Friday, January 24, 2014.
         </em>
        </p>
        <p>
         <a name="recipe">
         </a>
         <br/>
        </p>
        <div class="print-this-button-shell">
         <button class="print-this-button" onclick="parent.location='http://www.eatthelove.com/2014/01/korean-fried-chicken-recipe/?printthis=1&amp;printsect=1'" type="button">
          Print This
         </button>
        </div>
        <!-- Print This Section 1 Start -->
        <div class="print-this-content">
         <div itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Recipe">
          <h2>
           <span itemprop="name">
            Korean Fried Chicken Recipe
           </span>
          </h2>
          <p>
           By
           <span itemprop="author">
            Irvin Lin
           </span>
           <meta content="2014-01-21" itemprop="datePublished"/>
           <meta content="PT15M" itemprop="prepTime"/>
           <meta content="PT35M" itemprop="cookTime"/>
          </p>
          <p>
           <span itemprop="description">
            Unlike traditional fried chicken, which is batter dipped and fried, these chicken wings are tossed in a thin coating of egg white, salt and baking soda then they are dried out in the fridge overnight to be baked in the oven. The result is a super crisp-skinned chicken without the deep-frying, which means an easier clean up and cooking (no constantly checking the deep fryer!). The sauce requires a trip to the Asian grocery store to get gochujang, a Korean chile paste. Its a deep red fermented chili paste that has a nice deep dark flavor (not too much heat, with a little bit of sweetness). Youll have to refrigerate the chicken overnight to let the egg white coating dry so keep that in mind if you are planning to make these.
           </span>
          </p>
          <p>
           Adapted from
           <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0770433219/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=390957&amp;creativeASIN=0770433219&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=eathlo-20" target="_blank">
            Maximum Flavor
           </a>
           by Aki Kamozawa and Alexander H. Talbot and
           <a href="http://www.seriouseats.com/recipes/2012/10/sweet-and-spicy-chili-sauce-korean-fried-chicken-recipe.html" target="_blank">
            Serious Eats
           </a>
           .
          </p>
          <p>
           <em>
            [Editors Note: Numerous people have asked me where you can get gochujang. Amazon has
            <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B002WTE0MQ/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=390957&amp;creativeASIN=B002WTE0MQ&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=eathlo-20&amp;linkId=7ZUNRXBOFTUYDXKO" target="_blank">
             gochujang
            </a>
            though keep in mind its often cheaper to get it at an Asian grocery store if you can find it there. And if you are a looking for a gluten free option, check out
            <a href="http://www.werubyou.com/" target="_blank">
             We Rub Yous Hot Korean Gochujang Sauce
            </a>
            which is vegan and gluten free. I havent tried either gochujang I linked to, so I cant speak to how they taste but the Amazon one seems popular and the We Rub You sounds pretty good on (virtual) paper. Oh yeah, the above Amazon link is an affiliate link, so if you click through and buy it, I earn a small percentage off of the link. Feel free to just bounce directly to Amazon.com and search for gochujang if you want.]
           </em>
          </p>
          <p>
           <a href="http://www.eatthelove.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/Korean-Fried-Chicken-Recipe-3.jpg">
            <img alt="Korean Fried Chicken Recipe. Recipe and Photo by Irvin Lin of Eat the Love. www.eatthelove.com" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-10800" height="360" itemprop="image" onerror="this.onerror=null;pagespeed.lazyLoadImages.loadIfVisibleAndMaybeBeacon(this);" onload="pagespeed.lazyLoadImages.loadIfVisibleAndMaybeBeacon(this);" pagespeed_lazy_src="http://www.eatthelove.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/Korean-Fried-Chicken-Recipe-3.jpg" src="//1-ps.googleusercontent.com/hk/N7MgqQe61PieTxdAHj4St7PAZ5/www.gstatic.com/psa/static/1.gif" width="540"/>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p>
           <strong>
            Ingredients
           </strong>
           <br/>
           <span itemprop="ingredients">
            2 large egg whites
           </span>
           <br/>
           <span itemprop="ingredients">
            1 teaspoon sea salt
           </span>
           , finely ground
           <br/>
           <span itemprop="ingredients">
            1 teaspoon baking soda
           </span>
           <br/>
           <span itemprop="ingredients">
            2 lbs chicken wings
           </span>
           , drumettes and flats separated with tips discards or saved for stock
           <br/>
           <span itemprop="ingredients">
            4 medium garlic cloves
           </span>
           <br/>
           <span itemprop="ingredients">
            1-inch knob of fresh ginger
           </span>
           <br/>
           <span itemprop="ingredients">
            1/4 cup gochujang
           </span>
           (Korean chile paste)
           <br/>
           <span itemprop="ingredients">
            2 tablespoons dark soy sauce
           </span>
           <br/>
           <span itemprop="ingredients">
            1 tablespoon rice wine vinegar
           </span>
           <br/>
           <span itemprop="ingredients">
            3 tablespoon dark brown sugar
           </span>
           <br/>
           <span itemprop="ingredients">
            1 tablespoon Asian fish sauce
           </span>
           <br/>
           <span itemprop="ingredients">
            1 tablespoon toasted sesame oil
           </span>
          </p>
          <p>
           <strong>
            Special equipment
           </strong>
           <br/>
           Oven proof wire rack
           <br/>
           Rimmed baking sheet
          </p>
          <p>
           <strong>
            Directions
           </strong>
           <br/>
           <span itemprop="recipeInstructions">
            1. Place the wire rack inside a rimmed baking sheet. Place the egg whites, baking soda and sea salt in a large bowl and beat until the salt and baking soda is dissolved into the egg whites (feel the egg white, you shouldnt be able to feel any grains of salt). Toss the chicken wing pieces in the egg white mixture, making sure to coat all sides of the wings. Pick the wings up from the bowl, letting any excess egg white drip back in to the bowl, and put on the wire rack, making sure the wings arent touching. Put in the refrigerator, uncovered for 8 hours or overnight to dry out. If you can, flip the wings once to let both sides dry out evenly.
           </span>
          </p>
          <p>
           2. Once the wings have dried, preheat the oven to 450F. Place the wings (on the rack) in the oven for 15 minutes, then flip the wings over and bake for an additional 10 minutes. Flip one more time and bake for 10 more minutes or until the wings are crispy golden brown. Remove from oven and let rest for 5 minutes.
          </p>
          <p>
           3. While the chicken is baking, prepare the sauce by forcing the garlic through a garlic press or finely mincing it. Peel then finely grate the ginger. Place the garlic and ginger in large saut pan or wok and add the remaining ingredients (gochujang, soy sauce, rice wine vinegar, brown sugar, fish sauce and sesame oil). Once the wings come out from the oven, turn the heat to medium and cook the sauce until it starts to thicken slightly, about two or three minutes. Toss the still warm wings in the sauce and serve immediately.
          </p>
          <p>
           Makes about
           <span itemprop="recipeYield">
            12-16 medium sized wings
            <span>
             , enough for 4 to 6 people as appetizers.
            </span>
           </span>
          </p>
         </div>
         <p>
         </p>
         <div class="clear">
         </div>
        </div>
        <!-- Print This Section 1 End -->
        <p>

             January 22, 2014 at 5:15 pm
            </a>
           </span>
          </dt>
          <dd class="comment byuser comment-author-irvin bypostauthor even depth-2">
           <div class="format_text" id="comment-body-128600">
            <p>
             If you dont live near an Asian grocery store you can always order the gojuchang from
             <a href="http://www.amazon.com/s/ref=sr_kk_2?rh=i%3Aaps%2Ck%3Agochujang&amp;keywords=gochujang&amp;ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1390439514" rel="nofollow">
              Amazon
             </a>
             .
            </p>
            <p>
             And its true, finding room for the wings in the fridge is a pain! The original recipe actually called for 4 lbs of wings, placed on two pans/racks. I SO couldnt find room for two pans in my refrigerator!
            </p>
            <p>
             That said. Since its only for overnight, I just sort of moved things around and placed the wings on top of stuff. As long as the pan wasnt in danger of shifting around or falling it was all good. Though my partner was a bit surprised when he opened the fridge in the morning and saw a pan of raw chicken sitting out on the shelf!
            </p>

           Is the chili paste = Shiracha (or however you spell it)?  These look soooooooooooooo good!!
          </p>
          <p class="reply">
           <a class="comment-reply-link" href="/2014/01/korean-fried-chicken-recipe/?replytocom=128590#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm("comment-body-128590", "128590", "respond", "10797")'>

         <dl class="children">
          <dt class="comment byuser comment-author-irvin bypostauthor even depth-2 parent" id="comment-128599">
           <span class="avatar">
            <a href="http://www.eatthelove.com" rel="nofollow">
            </a>
           </span>
           <span class="comment_author">
            <a class="url" href="http://www.eatthelove.com" rel="external nofollow">
             Irvin
            </a>
           </span>
           <span class="comment_time">
            <a href="#comment-128599" rel="nofollow" title="Permalink to this comment">
             January 22, 2014 at 5:12 pm
            </a>
           </span>
          </dt>
          <dd class="comment byuser comment-author-irvin bypostauthor even depth-2 parent">
           <div class="format_text" id="comment-body-128599">
            <p>
             Nope. Sriracha is something different. Gochujang has a deeper savory flavor to it and is salty and a touch sweet too. Sriracha is more a straightforward hot flavor, with a vinegar tang to it. It usually comes in a red rectangular tub. If you cant find, you can always order a tub of it from
             <a href="http://www.amazon.com/s/ref=sr_kk_2?rh=i%3Aaps%2Ck%3Agochujang&amp;keywords=gochujang&amp;ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1390439514" rel="nofollow">
              Amazon
             </a>
             .
            </p>
            <p class="reply">
             <a class="comment-reply-link" href="/2014/01/korean-fried-chicken-recipe/?replytocom=128599#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm("comment-body-128599", "128599", "respond", "10797")'>

          <a href="#comment-128615" rel="nofollow" title="Permalink to this comment">
           January 22, 2014 at 6:47 pm
          </a>
         </span>
        </dt>
        <dd class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 parent">
         <div class="format_text" id="comment-body-128615">
          <p>
           In case of dire straits wherein gojujang simply cannot be found, is there a way of possibly fudging it with other ingredients to supply the heat/funk/sweetness?
          </p>
          <p class="reply">
           <a class="comment-reply-link" href="/2014/01/korean-fried-chicken-recipe/?replytocom=128615#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm("comment-body-128615", "128615", "respond", "10797")'>
            Reply
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
         <dl class="children">
          <dt class="comment byuser comment-author-irvin bypostauthor odd alt depth-2" id="comment-128617">
           <span class="avatar">
            <a href="http://www.eatthelove.com" rel="nofollow">
            </a>
           </span>
           <span class="comment_author">
            <a class="url" href="http://www.eatthelove.com" rel="external nofollow">
             Irvin
            </a>
           </span>
           <span class="comment_time">
            <a href="#comment-128617" rel="nofollow" title="Permalink to this comment">
             January 22, 2014 at 7:12 pm
            </a>
           </span>
          </dt>
          <dd class="comment byuser comment-author-irvin bypostauthor odd alt depth-2">
           <div class="format_text" id="comment-body-128617">
            <p>
             Thats a really good question. Gochujang is pretty integral to the sauce. Its a fermented sweet spicy sauce and it hard to make at home, though there are recipes out there that on the web that show you how to do it (like
             <a href="http://www.kimchimom.com/2011/12/homemade-kochujang-hot-red-pepper-paste/" rel="nofollow">
              Kimchi Moms version
             </a>
             ). It also requires letting it sit out and ferment so theres that. Of course the ingredients to make it pretty much require you to go to an Asian market anyway  one that would probably carry gochujang to begin with.
            </p>
            <p>
             That said, there is a
             <a href="http://www.hannaone.com/Recipe/kochujangreplacement.html" rel="nofollow">
              gochujang recipe substitution
             </a>
             online that seems fairly straightforward without all the homemade DIY fermentation. It uses miso paste to get the funky fermented taste so you can try it in place. That said, having never substituted it before, I cant guarantee how itll taste or turn out. But if you do try substituting out, come back and let me know how it turns out!
            </p>
            <p>
             Of course, it might just be easier to order
             <a href="http://www.amazon.com/s/?_encoding=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=390957&amp;field-keywords=gochujang&amp;linkCode=ur2&amp;rh=i%3Aaps%2Ck%3Agochujang&amp;sprefix=gochujang%2Caps%2C265&amp;tag=eathlo-20&amp;url=search-alias%3Daps" rel="nofollow">
              some online at Amazon.com
             </a>
             .
            </p>
            <p class="reply">
             <a class="comment-reply-link" href="/2014/01/korean-fried-chicken-recipe/?replytocom=128617#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm("comment-body-128617", "128617", "respond", "10797")'>
              Reply
             </a>
            </p>
           </div>

          <dd class="comment byuser comment-author-irvin bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 parent">
           <div class="format_text" id="comment-body-128642">
            <p>
             Im partial to Red Boat fish sauce which is made with anchovies and sea salt only (thats their only ingredients listed). In fact, their bottle says gluten free, no shellfish on it, so you should be safe. But if you cant find it, just leave the fish sauce out of the recipe. It adds a nice subtle depth and umami flavor to the sauce but it isnt totally necessarily.
            </p>
            <p>
             As for the soy sauce version, you could try the
             <a href="http://www.seriouseats.com/recipes/2012/10/sweet-soy-sauce-korean-fried-chicken-recipe.html" rel="nofollow">
              Serious Eats version
             </a>
             of the sweet soy sauce for their Korean Fried Chicken. Just leave out the crushed dried red pepper.
            </p>

          <dd class="comment byuser comment-author-irvin bypostauthor even depth-2">
           <div class="format_text" id="comment-body-129313">
            <p>
             I think so, but because the chicken leg is  larger than the wing, you should probably bake the chicken for longer  maybe an additional 15 minute more (for a total of an hour).
            </p>
            <p>
             But check the chicken after flipping it and baking for 15 minutes. Pierce a piece a leg with a thin skewer. If the juice runs out clear its done. If its pink, cook it longer. Or use a thermometer and cook it until 170F.
            </p>
            <p class="reply">
             <a class="comment-reply-link" href="/2014/01/korean-fried-chicken-recipe/?replytocom=129313#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm("comment-body-129313", "129313", "respond", "10797")'>

            <p>
             Gochujang isnt super spicy but there is a little heat. Its more a savory umami flavor with some heat and sweetness. Think red chili peppers or a tiny amount of cayenne mixed with miso paste.
            </p>

           <div class="format_text" id="comment-body-129317">
            <p>
             Ive never had Franks sweet Chili Sauce but my guess is no. Korean Guchujang is fermented so it definitely has a more earthy and savory depth to it that Ive not had it sweet or spicy American based chili sauces.
            </p>
            <p>
             But if you substitute Franks sweet chili sauce Im sure the wings will still be delicious. Just different! If you do it, let me know what you think!
            </p>

            <p>
             I think they wouldnt but Ive never done it. If you do try it with breasts or thighs, make sure to adjust the cooking time in the oven. You might also want to lower the temperature and bake longer. You dont want to burn the outside and still have raw chicken on the inside!
            </p>

          <p>
           How about grilling instead of baking?
          </p>
          <p class="reply">
           <a class="comment-reply-link" href="/2014/01/korean-fried-chicken-recipe/?replytocom=129278#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm("comment-body-129278", "129278", "respond", "10797")'>

         <dl class="children">
          <dt class="comment byuser comment-author-irvin bypostauthor odd alt depth-2" id="comment-129320">
           <span class="avatar">
            <a href="http://www.eatthelove.com" rel="nofollow">
            </a>
           </span>
           <span class="comment_author">
            <a class="url" href="http://www.eatthelove.com" rel="external nofollow">
             Irvin
            </a>
           </span>
           <span class="comment_time">
            <a href="#comment-129320" rel="nofollow" title="Permalink to this comment">
             January 27, 2014 at 2:17 am
            </a>
           </span>
          </dt>
          <dd class="comment byuser comment-author-irvin bypostauthor odd alt depth-2">
           <div class="format_text" id="comment-body-129320">
            <p>
             One of the signature parts of Korean Fried Chicken is the super crispy skin that you get when you double fry it, which is why I coat the wings with the egg white first and let it dry out before baking it.
            </p>
            <p>
             Because of that, if you grill it, youll just get a different sort of wing. Im sure itll still be delicious, but not the same as Korean Fried Chicken, baked or fried. If you do grill it, you might want to try making the sauce and basting the wings at the very end of you grilling them. They wont get the crispy outside but theyll have a smoky sweet spicy to them that Im sure would be great.
            </p>
            <p>
             Or try my
             <a href=" http://www.eatthelove.com/2014/01/korean-bbq-chicken-recipe/" rel="nofollow">
              Korean BBQ wings recipe
             </a>
             , which has instructions for grilling. They are different than the wings recipe above but also really tasty.
            </p>
            <p class="reply">
             <a class="comment-reply-link" href="/2014/01/korean-fried-chicken-recipe/?replytocom=129320#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm("comment-body-129320", "129320", "respond", "10797")'>
              Reply
             </a>
            </p>

          <p>
           I love your recipes. What is the substitue of rice wine vinegar if not available here in my place.
          </p>
          <p class="reply">
           <a class="comment-reply-link" href="/2014/01/korean-fried-chicken-recipe/?replytocom=129310#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm("comment-body-129310", "129310", "respond", "10797")'>

         <dl class="children">
          <dt class="comment byuser comment-author-irvin bypostauthor odd alt depth-2" id="comment-129322">
           <span class="avatar">
            <a href="http://www.eatthelove.com" rel="nofollow">
            </a>
           </span>
           <span class="comment_author">
            <a class="url" href="http://www.eatthelove.com" rel="external nofollow">
             Irvin
            </a>
           </span>
           <span class="comment_time">
            <a href="#comment-129322" rel="nofollow" title="Permalink to this comment">
             January 27, 2014 at 2:20 am
            </a>
           </span>
          </dt>
          <dd class="comment byuser comment-author-irvin bypostauthor odd alt depth-2">
           <div class="format_text" id="comment-body-129322">
            <p>
             Rice wine vinegar is a little more mild and slightly sweet, so Id just use white wine vinegar or or apple cider vinegar in its place. You might want to add a pinch of extra sugar as well to add the sweetness.
            </p>
            <p>
             If all you have regular white vinegar, add 2 teaspoons of it, and add 1 teaspoon of water to dilute it a bit as its a little stronger. And add the pinch of extra sugar.
            </p>
            <p class="reply">
             <a class="comment-reply-link" href="/2014/01/korean-fried-chicken-recipe/?replytocom=129322#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm("comment-body-129322", "129322", "respond", "10797")'>

          <p>
           Found the gochujang (Korean chile paste) in the fridge at my nearest Chinese supermarket! Now Im making these! How long does the gochujang (Korean chile paste) last once its opened????
          </p>
          <p class="reply">
           <a class="comment-reply-link" href="/2014/01/korean-fried-chicken-recipe/?replytocom=132912#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm("comment-body-132912", "132912", "respond", "10797")'>

          <dt class="comment byuser comment-author-irvin bypostauthor even depth-2" id="comment-133015">
           <span class="avatar">
            <a href="http://www.eatthelove.com" rel="nofollow">
            </a>
           </span>
           <span class="comment_author">
            <a class="url" href="http://www.eatthelove.com" rel="external nofollow">
             Irvin
            </a>
           </span>
           <span class="comment_time">
            <a href="#comment-133015" rel="nofollow" title="Permalink to this comment">
             February 18, 2014 at 7:05 pm
            </a>
           </span>
          </dt>
          <dd class="comment byuser comment-author-irvin bypostauthor even depth-2">
           <div class="format_text" id="comment-body-133015">
            <p>
             Your tub of gochujang should have an expiration date on it, but everything Ive read online says it lasts at least a year in the fridge if not longer. If you dont plan on using it within the year, you can freeze it but its pretty hardy. Theres a lot of salt, sugar and spices in there and all of those things act as natural preservatives
            </p>
            <p class="reply">
             <a class="comment-reply-link" href="/2014/01/korean-fried-chicken-recipe/?replytocom=133015#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm("comment-body-133015", "133015", "respond", "10797")'>

             </a>

           </span>
          </dt>
          <dd class="comment byuser comment-author-irvin bypostauthor even depth-2">
           <div class="format_text" id="comment-body-143641">
            <p>
             This coating is specifically designed for baking in the oven. Im not sure how it would work out with deep frying it. There are a number of deep fried versions of Korean Fried Chicken out there, just google Korean Fried Chicken recipe and they will pop up! Or you can try using the batter for my
             <a href="http://www.eatthelove.com/2014/01/pok-pok-wings-recipe/" rel="nofollow">
              Pok Pok chicken wings
             </a>
             , just skip the overnight fish sauce marinade if you plan on making them for Korean Fried Chicken. That particular batter is so crisp you dont need to double fry it.
            </p>
            <p class="reply">
             <a class="comment-reply-link" href="/2014/01/korean-fried-chicken-recipe/?replytocom=143641#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm("comment-body-143641", "143641", "respond", "10797")'>

        <li class="widget widget_text" id="text-5">
         <h3>
          The Baker, Writer, Recipe Maker
         </h3>
         <div class="textwidget">
          <p>
           <a href="mailto:eatthelove@gmail.com">
            <img src="http://www.eatthelove.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/irvin_eyebrow_mini2.jpg"/>
           </a>
          </p>
          <div align="left">
           Hey there! Thanks for visiting my blog. I'm Irvin Lin, an IACP-Award winning photographer, award winning baker,
           <a href="http://www.jackhonky.com/" target="_blank">
            award winning graphic designer
           </a>
           , storyteller, recipe developer, writer and average joe bon vivant. Hilarity often ensues when I'm involved. I currently reside in San Francisco in the neighborhood people have recently taken to calling "The Gastro" - a block from Dolores Park and right near Tartine Bakery, Bi Rite Market &amp; Creamery, and Delfina.
           <p>
            I can also be found at various food events around the city. Feel free to contact me by clicking on that picture of me up above or emailing me eatthelove {at} gmail {dot} com.
           </p>
          </div>
          <p>
          </p>

        <li class="widget widget_text" id="text-8">
         <div class="textwidget">
          <p>
           <img onerror="this.onerror=null;pagespeed.lazyLoadImages.loadIfVisibleAndMaybeBeacon(this);" onload="pagespeed.lazyLoadImages.loadIfVisibleAndMaybeBeacon(this);" pagespeed_lazy_src="http://www.eatthelove.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/Photography_Contest_BIS-3.png" src="//1-ps.googleusercontent.com/hk/N7MgqQe61PieTxdAHj4St7PAZ5/www.gstatic.com/psa/static/1.gif"/>
           <a href="http://www.saveur.com/article/Kitchen/Sites-We-Love-Eat-the-Love/">
            <img onerror="this.onerror=null;pagespeed.lazyLoadImages.loadIfVisibleAndMaybeBeacon(this);" onload="pagespeed.lazyLoadImages.loadIfVisibleAndMaybeBeacon(this);" pagespeed_lazy_src="http://www.eatthelove.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/Sites_We_Love_120.jpg" src="//1-ps.googleusercontent.com/hk/N7MgqQe61PieTxdAHj4St7PAZ5/www.gstatic.com/psa/static/1.gif" style="border:none;width:120px;height:120px"/>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p>
           Irvin Lin is the creative mind behind his
           <em>
            Eat the Love
           </em>
           food blog. Lins impressive photography skills support his training in graphic design on the site, and you would never believe that is food blogger is a self-taught baker. -
           <a href="http://www.pbs.org/food/features/11-food-blogs-we-liked-in-2011/7/">
            PBS Food
           </a>
          </p>
          <p>
           We love
           <i>
            Eat the Love
           </i>
           because Irvin's beautiful sweets look as good as they taste  his art director's eye appreciates the ruby sparkle of a pile of pomegranate seeds against the matte canvas of chocolate ganache.
           <br/>
           -
           <a href="http://www.saveur.com/article/Kitchen/Sites-We-Love-Eat-the-Love">
            Saveur.com
           </a>
           , Sites We Love
          </p>
          <p>
           Lin, a designer and baker, shares his passion for baking with creative sweets that focus on seasonal ingredients with healthy doses of humor and charm. It's impossible not to read his site and crave dessert.
           <br/>
           - Yum Food &amp; Fun Magazine
          </p>
         </div>
